
## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)

# Domain Lineage: Kafka Producer Config Propagation Path

## Your Task

Trace how the `acks` producer configuration value propagates through the Kafka codebase. Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that: 1. Define the `acks` configuration constant (in `ProducerConfig`). 2. Read and validate the `acks` value during producer initialization. 3. Encode the `acks` value into the produce request protocol (the `ProduceRequest` builder). 4. Apply the `acks` value in the broker-side partition leader to determine write acknowledgment behavior. Report the repo, file path, class name, and the role in the propagation chain for each file.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've successfully traced the complete propagation path of the `acks` producer configuration value through the Kafka codebase and created a comprehensive answer at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

The `acks` configuration flows through the following key stages:

1. **Definition** - `ProducerConfig.java` (line 123): Defines `ACKS_CONFIG` constant and validates allowed values (all, -1, 0, 1)

2. **Parsing & Validation** - `ProducerConfig.java` (lines 639-645): The `parseAcks` method converts the string value "all" to "-1" or validates numeric values

3. **Producer Initialization** - `KafkaProducer.java` (line 526): Reads and parses the acks value, passing it to the Sender

4. **Protocol Encoding** - `Sender.java` (line 899): Encodes acks into `ProduceRequestData` via `.setAcks(acks)`

5. **Request Building** - `ProduceRequest.java` (line 104): Stores acks value in the request object

6. **Broker Processing** - `KafkaApis.scala` (line 537): Passes acks to `ReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend` as `requiredAcks`

7. **Replication Coordination** - `ReplicaManager.scala` (lines 1355-1361): The `delayedProduceRequestRequired` method determines that only when `requiredAcks == -1` should the broker wait for replica acknowledgments

8. **Broker Enforcement** - `Partition.scala` (line 1370): When `requiredAcks == -1`, enforces min.isr requirement, throwing `NotEnoughReplicasException` if insufficient in-sync replicas exist

The answer includes all relevant files, symbols, and a detailed chain explaining each step's role in controlling whether the broker waits for none (acks=0), the leader (acks=1), or all in-sync replicas (acks=-1/all) before acknowledging writes.

This controls the \\\"\\n125:                                            + \\\" durability of records that are sent. The following settings are allowed: \\\"\\n126:                                            + \\\" <ul>\\\"\\n127:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=0</code> If set to zero then the producer will not wait for any acknowledgment from the\\\"\\n128:                                            + \\\" server at all. The record will be immediately added to the socket buffer and considered sent. No guarantee can be\\\"\\n129:                                            + \\\" made that the server has received the record in this case, and the <code>retries</code> configuration will not\\\"\\n130:                                            + \\\" take effect (as the client won't generally know of any failures). The offset given back for each record will\\\"\\n131:                                            + \\\" always be set to <code>-1</code>.\\\"\\n132:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=1</code> This will mean the leader will write the record to its local log but will respond\\\"\\n133:                                            + \\\" without awaiting full acknowledgement from all followers. In this case should the leader fail immediately after\\\"\\n134:                                            + \\\" acknowledging the record but before the followers have replicated it then the record will be lost.\\\"\\n135:                                            + \\\" <li><code>acks=all</code> This means the leader will wait for the full set of in-sync replicas to\\\"\\n136:                                            + \\\" acknowledge the record. This guarantees that the record will not be lost as long as at least one in-sync replica\\\"\\n137:                                            + \\\" remains alive. This is the strongest available guarantee. By default, when acks=all, acknowledgement happens as soon as all the current in-sync\n522:     replicas have received the message. For example, if a topic is configured with only two replicas and one fails (i.e., only one in sync replica remains), then writes that specify acks=all will succeed. However, these\n523:     writes could be lost if the remaining replica also fails.\n524: ",

            "content": "196:     <p>\n197:     Most messaging systems keep metadata about what messages have been consumed on the broker. That is, as a message is handed out to a consumer, the broker either records that fact locally immediately or it may wait\n198:     for acknowledgement from the consumer. This is a fairly intuitive choice, and indeed for a single machine server it is not clear where else this state could go. Since the data structures used for storage in many\n199:     messaging systems scale poorly, this is also a pragmatic choice--since the broker knows what is consumed it can immediately delete it, keeping the data size small.\n200:     <p>\n201:     What is perhaps not obvious is that getting the broker and consumer to come into agreement about what has been consumed is not a trivial problem. This means that the consumer need not worry about potentially seeing a message that could be lost if the leader fails. Producers, on the other hand,\n432:     have the option of either waiting for the message to be committed or not, depending on their preference for tradeoff between latency and durability.
